Grappling is a fun sport and can be useful in combat, but itâ€™s usually displayed as someone bending over and taking it from someone else. Can I reach your ears, eyes, hands or even your wrist if so you can be in for something worse than a beating, small joints and ligaments can be broken and damaged with a single hand grab. In order for someone to learn self defense grappling properly they should probably learn the brutalities of real self defense combat so they know how important the game of Iâ€™ve got your ear is. Just try playing with your own ear, but I wouldnâ€™t advise touching your eye. Letting people know that you can strike them is important as well. Grappling is a good tool, but what is a good tool if donâ€™t know how to apply it properly, itâ€™s a delusion about what the what someone will do to defend themselves. I used to be able to get out of a choke hold while standing, one of the submissions that doesnâ€™t require a bunch of setup on the ground it was easier to get out of and nearly impossible to get into. I donâ€™t know why so much half baked self defense gets taught to people itâ€™s dangerous, Iâ€™m sure they will learn more as they are training for combat. Now pretend youâ€™re trying to run away and escape like we are in an actual fight to the death, like someone in a horror movie, this idea usually helps people to realize if you are kicking and screaming that youâ€™re incredibly hard to get into a joint lock, but expels a lot of stamina.  The most effective fighting technique is to run away unless you are trapped or have someone or something to protect and it better be worth the risk.

Let me start out by saying Paddy is a beast! No one can take that away from him.  The big take-away from this is the importance of cross-discipline training. As a U.S. Marine, we are taught how to kill with maximum efficiency on the battlefield with boots, utility gear, a rifle, and full combat load, while applying KISS because we do not train consistently for 8-16 hours per week like a typical Judoka. The techniques must be deadly, but also simple enough to allow for less training and fog-of-war.    As a Jujitsu and Judo instructor, our 'waza' (techniques) are equally deadly/effective, but lack the violence, intensity and modern combat application. Rolling around on the battlefield for 5 minutes will get you killed by his buddy. Likewise, boot-stomping someone in the ally for trying to take your wallet will still end with you behind bars. Everyone is better off when we humble ourselves and seek out techniques that other disciplines have to offer.  ~ Semper Fi

Granted he did a lot better on the ground than I ever seen him do in the cage.. But we got to hold on a minute... Some of those Marines may have been in for a year or 2  And they don't train MCMAP everyday. MCMAP is  Marine Corps Marshall Arts Program.  It's a combination of judo, karate, and jujitsu primarily. Tan, Gray, green, brown, black  Is the order of our belts. If you're an instructor you'll get a red tab on your belt.    He did well and just to have the endurance to go through 10 rounds is tuff.   Honestly I think these Marines failed him because the best part of training is when you bring it in. The instructor will tell you a story about on this day many years ago  how somebody did something amazing. That's the most motivating shit you could fucking ever imagine. When you're dead tired and  you hear about how this man saved somebody's life or gave his own.  As we said in bootcamp every night  Before we hit The rack. Biggest thing for me regarding mental health & talking to people about mine, is i thought i needed to go the docs knowing in my head exactly what made me constantly sad, but through many hours of professional help i found it wasn't any single thing that i could identify & address.  It was an accumulation of so many things, most i'd consider not worthy of mentioning, others to do with the environment i grew up in that moulded my personality in a negative way. It took many hours with a professional and total surrender by me to tease the causes out. *Don't put it off trying to convince yourself it's normal or it'll blow over, it doesn't, depression will put you in denial, consuming you while making you draw back from friends & loves ones*  not happy with your gp/docs response? find another.  I left it far too long, only when i hit rock bottom after dulling my emotions with booze & hard drugs for 10+ years. Having a friend i could have discussed such things without fear of ridicule would have been so invaluable, you couldn't put a price on it.   I still can't quite picture it, as anytime i try to be real with '' friends '' they swerve it and stick to the hard shell they wear to face the world,  can be hard not to think 'everyone is fake & resent every cunt coming into my orbit', that's where i am most days.    I try to focus on being that guy i needed, for my teenage sons.    Most importantly *don't be me, don't put off getting help,* given long enough it will shape who you are, I'm still a miserable fucker but living is bearable & my now wife attests that i'm so much nicer to be around.

This is the difference between ground game and fighting standing. Sure it's more exciting for most people, but punching and kicking is a roulette situation every time, regardless the opponents. Almost anyone can throw a strike and damage another, but if you are on the ground most untrained people do not know how to damage or threaten to submit. So then it's just a matter of time before the trained fighter wins, and it's usually much faster being that the attack and defense is a mystery.

Thus the light shined on the new days ahead to be where I am today. The best thing is after I had cut 110lbs (pushing for the last 30lbs for super middleweight) I had to stop my training after running into medical issues. It hurt, but when the dust settled I had myself and an amazing girlfriend who believed in me as her champion.  My journey was being noticed by others and from social media clips and I had those reach out to me commending me for my dedication in training and my all out war that I had with myself and how I handled it even so I know my suicide awareness segments hit home, even though no more than a few hundred people heard/had seen my story. It's funny, I had a bad run in with some serious anxiety problems when I was much younger, around 7th grade. I used to cry and fear waking up until it was 4am and I was down the hall waking my mother up. I ended up in therapy and while I didn't consider everything that I was suggested very impactful, I was asked to reach out to some adults or close friends that I was close with and fill them in on how I had been feeling and why I was so worried about this as an issue. I told my parents, I told my brother, I told my closest friends, my closest teachers at school, and at the end of that all, I immediately felt more understood. I felt as though if something did come up I had people that would help me get out of a situation before I panicked, even just knowing that was true put me on the path to getting out of that hole.
